2026-05-05 20:55:00 - integration finding: workspace cargo test caught a non-deterministic failure in module_swap_preserves_counter_state — `entity_id_to_i64` masked low 64 bits of ULID (id.ulid().0 & 0x0000_0000_ffff_ffff_ffff_ffff) which yielded a NEGATIVE i64 ~50% of the time. The wat fixtures use `i64.lt_s 0` as their "uninitialized handle" sentinel, so negative handles caused `tick` to early-return without mutating Counter. Agent had got lucky with positive ULIDs in their test runs.
2026-05-05 21:00:00 - orchestrator inline fix: changed entity_id_to_i64 mask to 0x7fff_ffff_ffff_ffff (low 63 bits) — guarantees non-negative i64 result. Verified stable: swap_smoke passed 5/5 reruns. (One bit of entity-distinguishing entropy lost; 2^63 distinct handles still vastly more than any conceivable scene.)

2026-05-06 19:35:00 - new file crates/cad-core/src/operators/extrude.rs (670 lines = 405 impl + 265 tests). Polygon2D struct: closed 2D polygon in XY plane (implicit close); pub fn new(points) validates ≥3 points + finite + no coincident-adjacent points returning Polygon2DError::{TooFewPoints, NonFiniteCoordinate, DegenerateEdge}; pub(crate) fn signed_area() via shoelace formula; pub(crate) fn convexity() returns Some(true) if all adjacent-edge cross-products have same sign, Some(false) if not, None if all collinear. ExtrudeOp { profile: Polygon2D, length: f32 } arity=0 (profile is parameter, NOT upstream input — same convention as CuboidOp). evaluate() validates length finite>0, profile valid, signed_area != 0, convexity == Some(true) (concave rejected with InvalidParameter matching "convex"); CW input handled internally by reversing iteration order so algorithm always sees CCW. Vertex generation: 2n verts (n bottom z=0, n top z=length). Fan triangulation from vertex 0 for both caps with proper outward-facing winding (bottom -Z normal via reversed indices, top +Z normal via natural indices). Side walls: 2 triangles per ring edge. Total triangle count = 4n-4 = 2(n-2) cap tris + 2n side tris. structural_hash = BLAKE3 over (b"extrude:" || length.to_le_bytes() || profile_len_u32 || profile_points_le_bytes).

2026-05-06 21:05:00 - new file crates/cad-core/src/operators/revolve.rs (526 lines). RevolveOp { profile: Polygon2D, segments: u32 } arity=0 (profile + segments are parameters, NOT upstream inputs — same convention as Cuboid/Extrude). RevolveOp::new validates segments >= 3 returning InvalidParameter("segments must be >= 3"); evaluate() validates profile.len() ≥ 3 + all points finite + all x >= 0 (profile lies on +X side of Y-axis) + signed_area != 0; concave profiles ALLOWED for full revolution (no fan-triangulated caps needed → Extrude's convexity restriction does NOT apply to Revolve). CW input handled by reversing iteration order so algorithm always processes CCW. Algorithm: full 2π rotation around Y-axis with `segments` rotational steps; per profile point (x,y) at ring s with θ = s*(2π/segments), 3D position = (x*cos θ, y, x*sin θ). Total n*segments vertices, 2*n*segments triangles via 2 tris per profile-edge per segment-quad. No caps — full revolution closes on itself via index wrap (s+1) % segments. Side-wall winding (a,b,c)+(a,c,d) emits outward radial normal verified by revolve_first_quad_has_outward_radial_normal unit test on triangle profile [(1,0),(2,0),(1,1)] at s=0,p=0. structural_hash = BLAKE3 over (b"revolve:" || segments.to_le_bytes() || profile_len_u32 || profile_points_le_bytes).

2026-05-06 22:00:00 - D-BOOLEAN CSG LIBRARY SCOPING ADR research dispatch (read-only — zero Rust changes)
2026-05-06 22:25:00 - new file docs/adr/ADR-112-cad-boolean-csg-library.md (196 lines, 14 sections — Context / 4 Options / Decision / Consequences (Positive + Negative + Mitigations) / Alternatives explicitly NOT chosen / Implementation guidance / Followups + open questions). FIRST ADR landed in workspace — docs/adr/ was empty before.
2026-05-06 22:26:00 - Decision: csgrs (Option 1 — pure-Rust BSP-tree triangle-mesh CSG) over parry (rejected: doesn't perform mesh booleans, only spatial queries / convex-hull / ACD), truck (rejected: would force migrating all 4 existing operators from Tessellation to Solid; deferred to a future ADR-113 placeholder), and roll-our-own (rejected: 1500 LoC budget vs csgrs's 5+ years of edge-case fixes; csg.js reference is 538 LoC of JavaScript, idiomatic Rust port ≈ 600-750 LoC algorithm + 400-600 LoC tests — credible upper bound but unjustified vs taking the dep).
2026-05-06 22:27:00 - csgrs status (per ADR research): v0.20.1 (Jul 2025), MIT, single maintainer (timschmidt), 9 releases / 969 commits. Direct deps: nalgebra 0.34, geo 0.29, hashbrown 0.15, robust 1.1, thiserror 2.0, either; optional parry3d / rapier3d / earcutr / spade / chull. README explicitly lists T-junction handling as TODO — known fragility class for downstream rendering and Phase 7.4 lineage. Does NOT declare forbid(unsafe_code).

2026-05-07 07:00:00 - Complications encountered: csgrs Polygon<S>::metadata is Option<S>; dispatch's algorithm draft suggested input_count < output_count → Merged but in practice csgrs's BSP retriangulation produces input < output for surviving partially-consumed faces (e.g., 2 input tris → 9 output tris on the same plane label) — naively classifying that as Merged would re-introduce the v0 false-positive. Resolution: refined the algorithm so any same-label count mismatch is classified as Split on the labeled path (Merged remains reachable through multi-input-label collapse, which is unobservable from per-input-label scan). This matches the dispatch's success criterion ("at least one Split edge surfaces") and the Goal section's intent.

2026-05-08 14:15:00 - ADR-114-pluginctx-owned-handoff.md (162L). Documents kernel/plugin-host's PluginContext v1 (CRITICAL #2) + audit-2 Phase 0 catch_unwind hardening as a unified design rationale. Decision: BTreeMap<TypeId, Box<dyn Any + Send>> registry; plugins take<T>/insert<T>; orchestrator wraps every call in std::panic::catch_unwind(AssertUnwindSafe(...)) + pre/post BTreeSet<TypeId> snapshots for leak detection. **No unsafe** is load-bearing for unsafe_code = forbid pledge. 5-variant PluginError taxonomy (InitFailed / ShutdownFailed / RuntimeFault / ContractViolation / Panic{phase, payload}) with PluginPhase enum. Rejected alternatives: borrowed-refs (requires unsafe), generic context types (combinatorial explosion across dogfood plugins), capability-based runtime context (orthogonal — could layer on top). First canary: cad-projection::CadProjectionPlugin (16 tests). Followup: gfx::Plugin canary (proves design generalizes).

Added Check 2: detect `BTreeMap<K, BTreeSet<K>>` and `HashMap<K, HashSet<K>>` struct field shapes where outer key type matches inner set's element type — the canonical adjacency-map "graph reinvention" pattern. False-positive guard: BTreeMap<UserId, BTreeSet<Permission>> NOT flagged (different types); only K==V triggers. v1 scope: struct fields only (not function args / locals / wrapped types like Arc<BTreeMap<K, BTreeSet<K>>>).

2026-05-09 05:10:00 - Deliverable 2 (physics local AuditLedger stub migration): **STOPPED with clean divergence report**. Decision-tree branch (b): non-trivial API divergence detected. Local `crate::stubs::audit_ledger::AuditLedger` records physics-domain `PhysicsInput { Force | Impulse | JointMotor }` into per-tick `TickRecord`s; surface = `records: Vec<TickRecord>` + `begin_tick(tick) -> &mut TickRecord` + `for_tick(tick) -> Option<&TickRecord>`. Kernel substrate `rge_kernel_audit_ledger::AuditLedger` is generic event ledger: `Event { id, seq, timestamp_ms, kind: EventKind, payload: Vec<u8> }` with content-addressed BLAKE3 EventId + undo/redo cursor; `EventKind = { Action, CadCheckpoint, Custom(String) }` — no physics-input variant. Production `step.rs` directly manipulates `ledger.records.last_mut().expect(...).inputs.push(...)` against the local stub's structural API. No API-compatible swap. Three migration paths surfaced (orchestrator decision pending): (a) migrate physics step.rs onto `EventKind::Custom("PhysicsInput")` with serialized TickRecord payload (touches step.rs / apply_force / apply_impulse / apply_recorded_inputs / determinism-replay test; changes on-disk shape); (b) keep local impl permanently but RENAME from `stubs::audit_ledger::AuditLedger` to `physics::PhysicsInputLedger` to stop presenting it as a "stub" of the kernel ledger (lightest-touch close; formalizes that physics has its own domain ledger separate from the engine-wide event ledger; ADR-114 amendment table footnote becomes "physics intentionally uses its own domain ledger PhysicsInputLedger, NOT the kernel/audit-ledger generic event ledger"); (c) extend kernel/audit-ledger with first-class per-tick / typed-payload abstractions (substrate change, broader scope). **Recommendation: option (b)** — closes audit-1 carryover finding without forcing a structural migration. The "stub" framing was misleading from W11; physics needs a per-tick physics-domain ledger which is structurally different from a generic event ledger.

2026-05-09 16:55:00 - **Critical design finding** (escalation-flagged + handled): rapier3d::World::serialize_state is NOT a full state snapshot — it's a per-body replay-equality digest hashing (idx, pos, rot, linvel, angvel, sleep) for byte-equality between replay runs; deliberately omits broadphase / island state; has NO inverse deserialize_state. CANNOT be used for SnapshotParticipate. The proper pattern: rapier3d 0.32 has its own `serde-serialize` Cargo feature (separate from `enhanced-determinism`; the two are NOT mutually exclusive — rapier3d/src/lib.rs only forbids the SIMD ↔ enhanced-determinism combo). The standard rapier-snapshot pattern (per https://rapier.rs/docs/user_guides/rust/serialization/) is to wrap all persistent fields in a struct, EXCEPT PhysicsPipeline whose own source comment reads "this contains only workspace data, so there is no point in making this serializable" — reconstructed via PhysicsPipeline::new() at restore time.

2026-05-10 00:30:00 - CHATGPT CROSS-REVIEW NOTE 2026-05-10 — POST-ROUND-6 ASSESSMENT (user-shared; archived per audit-1 precedent where the 2026-05-07 cross-review on capability-based context was cited inline in ADR-114). Cross-review's framing elevates several round-6 closures + identifies 3-priority next sequence.

**Architectural positioning (NEW — extends PLAN §0.2 moat statement)**: cross-review reframes RGE as "deterministic reactive CAD runtime with engine characteristics" rather than "game engine with CAD features". Long-term competitive frame shifts from Bevy/Fyrox toward Houdini / Siemens Parasolid / Autodesk Fusion / Blender Geometry Nodes / Open Cascade Technology — "but with deterministic replay + ECS-native orchestration + topology lineage + semantic constraints + pluginized kernels". Worth preserving as architectural context for future sessions / prospective contributors.

**Strongest round-6 success per cross-review**: 3-way PIE envelope byte-identity (cross_substrate_determinism.rs::pie_three_participant_round_trip_50_iter) — characterized as foundational for "deterministic collaborative CAD / authoritative simulation / undo-redo lineage / distributed replay / reproducible procedural pipelines" + "very few engines even attempt this level of determinism validation". Local audit framing was just "audit-closure"; cross-review elevates to strategic differentiator. The cross-format envelope byte-identity (RON + postcard + postcard interleave) is the load-bearing claim.

**Strongest round-6 architectural decision per cross-review**: #[non_exhaustive] hardening on PluginError / OpKind / TopologyEvolution. Cross-review: "classic future-explosion enums; without this, downstream crates freeze your ABI shape, semver pressure becomes catastrophic, operator roadmap becomes constrained, topology evolution becomes impossible to extend safely. You hardened the architectural growth surface before ecosystem lock-in. That is mature systems engineering." Round-6 H1 closure was rated as load-bearing more than I had framed.

**Strongest "hidden" architectural success per cross-review**: multi-canary composition test (multi_canary_integration.rs) is "more important than it looks" — proves "abstraction surfaces are probably genuinely orthogonal", which cross-review notes is hard ("many engines accidentally create hidden resource coupling / implicit lifecycle ordering / serialization leakage / subsystem ownership contamination"). Round-6 C3 closure was rated as a major architectural milestone vs my framing of "audit gap closure".

**Cross-review priority order for remaining items** (matches my ultra-deep round-6 deferred list almost exactly):
1. **H3 fault-injection harness** — "single most important architectural gap" per cross-review. Systematic chaos testing: panic injection / resource theft / partial initialization failure / double shutdown / corrupted snapshot payloads / stale topology references / replay divergence / allocator pressure. Without this "the runtime cannot become truly robust".
2. **C1 graph metrics implementation** — "strategically important". Currently 5-line stub at tools/graph-metrics/src/main.rs; PLAN §1.10.4 lists 10 metrics. Cross-review: "Eventually it becomes core infrastructure for rebuild optimization / probabilistic recovery / topology confidence / invalidation propagation / semantic dependency pruning / future AI-assisted CAD repair".
3. **M4 panic shield around ctx.insert** — "low probability does NOT mean low importance. Once third-party plugins exist somebody will panic mid-reinsertion; eventually resource graph corruption will happen; debugging will become horrific. You are approaching the scale where catch_unwind around substrate boundaries becomes mandatory infrastructure." Round-6 framed as "low-likelihood gap"; cross-review elevates to "rare but catastrophic corruption class".

**Architectural maturity assessment per cross-review** (post-round-6): ECS/runtime core = strong experimental; plugin substrate = early production-grade direction; CAD operator architecture = advanced prototype; deterministic infrastructure = exceptionally strong for stage; reflection/tooling = incomplete; editor architecture = pre-stabilization; fault isolation = partially mature; GPU abstraction = early; multi-user/distributed future readiness = surprisingly strong; kernel-grade topology infrastructure = emerging. Overall: "no longer looks like a hobby architecture experiment; now looks like a serious long-horizon runtime platform under active systems-engineering discipline." Round-6 closure shifted maturity dimensions: round-6 multi-canary integration moved plugin substrate from "isolated demos" to "compositional stability evidence"; round-6 #[non_exhaustive] hardening moved SemVer awareness to "high"; round-6 3-way PIE composition validated runtime determinism as "very high". Three subsystems remain meaningfully behind: reflection/tooling / editor architecture / GPU abstraction — these are next-session targets.

Pristine bytes still parse post-corruption (proves from_bytes doesn't mutate input on error path).

Recovery proof: remap_entity + re-tick succeeds + post-recovery orphan list empty (failure is genuinely recoverable per PLAN §13.12).
  - **`replay_divergence_byte_flip_detected_by_assertion`**: meta-test of physics determinism gate sensitivity. Two fresh 100-tick replays byte-identical (baseline). 4 corruption probes (flip middle / first / last byte; pop one byte) each MUST fire `assert_ne!(corrupted, cap2)`. Proves gate is sensitive across all positions + length divergence (defends against future regressions where gate accidentally becomes prefix/suffix-only).

2026-05-10 02:00:00 - CHATGPT CROSS-REVIEW NOTE 2026-05-10 #2 — C1 GRAPH-METRICS ARCHITECTURAL DESIGN GUIDANCE (user-shared; archived alongside cross-review #1 in same-day pair). This cross-review was the design-session input that the prior cross-review flagged as needed before C1 implementation could begin. **Reframes C1 from "graph-metrics-as-utility" to "kernel's semantic-introspection nervous system"**: substrate placement is kernel-level not tools-level; determinism requirements are replay-stable; ABI care matters because consumers will be editor + Tier-3 plugins + future cloud orchestrator.

**Critical design pivot — "catastrophic later" warning about ad-hoc full-graph scans**: metrics MUST be event-sourced + snapshot-versioned + tier-stratified, or the subsystem itself becomes a runtime liability. Cross-review framing: "Do NOT compute metrics ad hoc from full graph scans. That becomes catastrophic later. You want incremental metrics / deterministic accumulation / event-driven updates / stable snapshot semantics. Otherwise rebuild latency explodes / reactive pipelines stall / editor responsiveness dies / distributed synchronization becomes difficult."

**3-tier metrics architecture** (cross-review's recommended split):
- **Tier A — O(1) incremental counters** (cheap, mutation-triggered, transactional). Examples: `node_count` / `edge_count` / `operator_count` / `constraint_count` / `invalidation_count`. Stored directly in graph state. Cheapest to implement; lands first.
- **Tier B — Incremental structural metrics** (maintained during graph mutations; partial recomputation only around affected regions). Examples: `max_depth` / `average fanout` / `SCC count` / `dependency diameter` / `topology lineage breadth`.
- **Tier C — Expensive analytical metrics** (background or explicit analysis pass only; NEVER compute synchronously inside hot mutation paths). Examples: entropy estimates / rebuild instability prediction / semantic volatility / probabilistic recovery confidence / graph centrality.

**Critical invariant — metrics must be snapshot-versioned**:
```rust
GraphMetrics {
    graph_revision: RevisionId,
    metrics_revision: RevisionId,
}
```
Otherwise: metrics become nondeterministic / replay integrity breaks / editor overlays drift / distributed comparison becomes invalid.

**Strong recommendation — event-sourced metric updates**:
```rust
enum GraphEvent {
    NodeAdded, NodeRemoved,
    EdgeAdded, EdgeRemoved,
    ConstraintAdded,
    OperatorExecuted,
    TopologySplit,
}
```
Metrics subscribe to event streams. Advantages: deterministic / replayable / testable / parallelizable later / serialization-friendly. Aligns with existing replay architecture (kernel/audit-ledger event-sourcing precedent).

**Module split** (cross-review's recommended directory structure):
```
graph-metrics/
    core/
    structural/
    topology/
    invalidation/
    recovery/
    analytics/
```
Rationale: monolithic metrics systems become impossible to evolve. Eventually some metrics become editor-only / runtime-only / CI-only / debugging-only / probabilistic-heuristic.

**4 highest-long-term-value future metric categories** (cross-review):
1. **Invalidation propagation pressure** — measures how expensive changes become; critical for reactive rebuild scheduling / incremental evaluation / viewport responsiveness.
2. **Topology volatility** — measures how unstable semantic identity is; critical for persistent references / topology lineage / downstream operator survivability; **highly differentiated infrastructure**.
3. **Constraint tension/conflict density** — measures how close graph is to instability; useful for solver optimization / predictive repair / AI-assisted diagnostics.
4. **Semantic entropy** — probably the most important research-oriented metric; estimates graph disorder / intent degradation / reconstruction difficulty / repair ambiguity; connects to probabilistic recovery / intent graphs / semantic constraints.

**Recommended 7-phase rollout** (do NOT build all 10 at once):
1. Tier A counters
2. Structural incremental metrics
3. Revision/version integration
4. Event sourcing
5. Analytical metrics
6. Editor visualization
7. Predictive/recovery metrics

**Engineering constraints** (load-bearing): metrics must be optional / feature-gated / alloc-aware / deterministic / serialization-safe. Otherwise metrics infrastructure itself becomes a runtime liability.

**Cross-review's overall assessment**: "C1 is no longer 'missing utility functionality.' It is the beginning of semantic runtime introspection infrastructure. Handled correctly, this subsystem becomes foundational for reactive CAD / distributed CAD / deterministic rebuilds / topology repair / AI-assisted modeling / graph optimization / future cloud/runtime orchestration."

**Action**: archive in change.md (this entry) + draft ADR-115 capturing binding architectural decisions before details fade. Implementation deferred until ready to start phase 1 (Tier A counters as transactional O(1) updates inside `kernel/graph-foundation::Graph<N, E>`).

Brief: capture binding architectural decisions for the graph-metrics subsystem before details fade; mirror ADR-098/104/114 structural quality.

2026-05-10 07:00:00 - CHATGPT CROSS-REVIEW NOTE 2026-05-10 #5 — PATH-C VALIDATION + PROTOCOL CONSOLIDATION PHASE FRAMING (user-shared; archived as 5th 2026-05-10 cross-review). Cross-review reinforces Path-C as correct + identifies the architecture phase + flags emerging risks + prescribes next-session sequencing constraint.

**Path-C validation**: cross-review confirms ADR-116 + CanaryPlugin trait formalization avoided BOTH failure modes simultaneously: (1) under-formalizing an emerging governance invariant; (2) over-engineering a premature plugin meta-system. Most important architectural decisions per cross-review were the things NOT added: no `CanaryTelemetry` / no registration system / no lifecycle framework / no macro layer / no reflection coupling / no scheduler hooks. "That restraint is a major positive signal."

**Strongest technical decisions endorsed**:
1. **`pub trait CanaryPlugin: Plugin`** super-trait extension over external/parallel design — preserves plugin-host authority + existing plugin contracts + future composability + trait-object interoperability + subsystem isolation; avoids "parallel plugin universe" fragmentation.
2. **Avoiding `const PLUGIN_ID: PluginId` on the trait** — would have broken trait object ergonomics + pushed generics unnecessarily + encouraged compile-time overcoupling + conflicted with intended governance role. "Disciplined compromise mature Rust architectures require."
3. **Acceptance-test pattern** (instantiate → `&dyn CanaryPlugin` → assert zero state) — "deceptively important; validates dyn dispatch viability + object safety + uniform protocol conformance + deterministic initialization semantics + governance-level compatibility without introducing integration coupling."

**Most important long-term outcome reframed**: the trait is small but the INVARIANT is large. Cross-review framing: "telemetry increments ONLY on semantically successful advancement" is the real payload of ADR-116, not the trait itself. Becomes foundational for replay determinism / scheduler observability / rollback safety / distributed execution / remote orchestration / analytics correctness / editor-runtime synchronization / eventual speculative execution. Cross-review: "This is why H5 turned out larger than expected."

**Audio naming drift discovery characterized as "valuable"**: cross-review notes this is exactly the class of issue future audits should prioritize — semantic vocabulary divergence / vocabulary divergence / stale authority surfaces / naming inconsistency / governance/source-of-truth mismatch. "Tiny fix. High leverage." Closing it immediately prevents future ADR confusion / plugin vocabulary bifurcation / telemetry naming fragmentation / editor-runtime terminology divergence. Cross-review: "you are now operating at the level where names / invariants / semantics / governance consistency matter more than mechanics. That is a meaningful maturity transition."

**Architecture phase named**: **Protocol Consolidation Phase**. Typical signs per cross-review: repeated subsystem shapes emerge / governance abstractions stabilize / semantic contracts become explicit / audits become invariant-focused / tooling feasibility increases / architectural vocabulary hardens. "Distinct from early experimentation / subsystem invention / raw feature expansion." The shift: "you are no longer mainly discovering what exists. You are deciding what is canonical / what is invariant / what is allowed to diverge / what becomes architectural law."

- **Next architecture milestone**: (1) M2 editor-ui canary under ADR-116 — first new canary adopting the formalized contract

2026-05-10 07:30:00 - CHATGPT CROSS-REVIEW NOTE 2026-05-10 #6 — DISPATCH 2 DOCTRINE-HARDENING DIRECTIVE FOR ADR-115 PHASE-2.5 (user-shared; archived as 6th 2026-05-10 cross-review). Reframes Dispatch 2 from "implementation sprint" to "doctrine-hardening session". Substantive design guidance with binding deliverable shape.

**Architectural question underneath ADR-115 phase-2.5**: "Which graph metrics are semantically incremental runtime telemetry versus analytically derived inspection products?" **Boundary-definition problem, not metrics problem.**

**Why this dispatch matters**: formalizes separation between (1) Runtime-native metrics — cheap, continuously maintained, scheduler-compatible, mutation-local; (2) Analytical metrics — potentially global, recomputed, traversal-heavy, inspection-oriented. Foundational for editor responsiveness / replay determinism guarantees / distributed evaluation scheduling / async graph analysis / tooling isolation / snapshot semantics / incremental rebuild economics. "If this boundary remains fuzzy, future systems accumulate hidden complexity debt."

**Reclassification logic per cross-review**:
- **Tier-B (incremental / runtime-native)**: node_count / edge_count / local fanout / mutation-local counters / append-only structural deltas. Characteristics: O(1) or mutation-local maintenance / deterministic update path / scheduler-friendly / naturally incremental.
- **Tier-C (analytical / on-demand)**: SCC count / graph diameter / max depth / global reachability / transitive closure-style metrics. Characteristics: traversal-heavy / potentially graph-global / unstable incremental economics / expensive invalidation semantics / scheduler-hostile if maintained eagerly. **"Those are analytical products, not runtime-native counters."**

**Anti-pattern warning** (load-bearing): do NOT optimize prematurely for "everything incremental" / "live metrics" / "always-hot graph analytics". That path produces invalidation hell / scheduler coupling / hidden recomputation cascades / fragile cache semantics / replay instability / editor-runtime entanglement. **"You want explicit semantic separation instead."**

**Recommended ADR-115 phase-2.5 amendment structure** (4 sections):

1. **Metric Taxonomy** — formalize: Tier-A = canonical structural counters; Tier-B = mutation-local incremental runtime metrics; Tier-C = analytical/on-demand derived metrics.

2. **Execution Semantics** — explicit:
   - Tier-C metrics are NOT scheduler-maintained
   - Tier-C metrics may require whole-graph traversal
   - Tier-C metrics are tooling / editor / inspection-oriented
   - **Tier-C metrics are NOT part of deterministic runtime advancement state** (load-bearing claim)

3. **Invalidation Model**: "Tier-C analytical metrics are invalidated structurally and recomputed on-demand rather than eagerly maintained." Avoids future accidental obligations.

4. **Snapshot Semantics**: clarify whether snapshots serialize Tier-C outputs OR only canonical graph state. **Strong recommendation: snapshot canonical state only; recompute Tier-C analytically.** Otherwise snapshots become polluted with derived-state synchronization obligations.

**Terminology precision** flagged as critical: must begin distinguishing runtime / analytical / observational / canonical / derived / deterministic / advisory. "These words are starting to carry architectural weight."

**Deliverable shape**:
- **Mandatory**: ADR-115 amendment (tier taxonomy clarification + explicit Tier-C semantics + on-demand computation doctrine + invalidation semantics)
- **Probably**: minimal implementation adjustments (lazy analytical execution paths / scheduler-decoupling comments+docs)
- **Avoid**: caching frameworks / async analytics infra / graph-analysis scheduler / persistent analytical state / "smart" invalidation systems. **"Too early."**

**Emerging architectural pattern named**: separating "Canonical Runtime Truth" FROM "Analytical Interpretation Layers". Important for deterministic replay / editor architecture / distributed runtime / collaborative tooling / eventual cloud execution / speculative rebuild systems. **"Many engines never formalize this cleanly. You are approaching it early enough to avoid substantial future debt."**

**Sequencing constraint** (binding): keep Dispatch 2 narrowly about metric semantics + execution boundaries + runtime-vs-analytical doctrine + invalidation philosophy + scheduler contract clarification. Do NOT combine with editor canary work / tooling architecture / GPU abstraction / reflection systems. "That boundedness is what will keep the architecture coherent as the protocol layer expands."

**Action**: archive cross-review #6 in change.md (this entry) + dispatch ADR-115 amendment per the 4-section structure + minimal docstring tier-tagging on existing graph-foundation methods (Tier-A/B classification flags) + zero new code-paths for Tier-C (those land when consumers materialize).

2026-05-09 18:00:00 - **D-7.2-δ Loft B-Rep face-identity (two-input local-provider)** landed as a bounded substrate dispatch in `crates/cad-core/src/topology/{face_tag,face_id,mod}.rs` + `crates/cad-core/src/operators/loft.rs` + `crates/cad-core/src/lib.rs` + new `crates/cad-core/tests/loft_face_identity_smoke.rs`. Adds the fourth `BRepProvider` impl — `LoftOp` — exercising the **two-input local-provider** topology axis. New `LoftFaceTag` 3-variant `#[non_exhaustive]` enum (`Bottom = 0`, `Top = 1`, `Side { edge_index: u32, profile_a_count: u32, profile_b_count: u32 } = 2`) in canonical face-emission order matching `LoftOp::evaluate` (Bottom cap → Top cap → Side(0..N-1)). New constructor `BRepFaceId::for_loft_face(owner, tag)` with operator-kind separator `b"loft:"` + appended `edge_index.to_le_bytes() || profile_a_count.to_le_bytes() || profile_b_count.to_le_bytes()` for `Side` only (caps' BLAKE3 input ends after the discriminant byte). New `KIND_LOFT: &'static [u8] = b"loft:"` const alongside existing `KIND_CUBOID` / `KIND_EXTRUDE` / `KIND_REVOLVE`. New additive `impl BRepProvider for LoftOp` block (~70L) returning `N + 2` pairs (`(TopologyFaceId(0), Bottom)`, `(TopologyFaceId(1), Top)`, `(TopologyFaceId(2 + i), Side { i, n_a, n_b })` for `i in 0..n` where `n = n_a.min(n_b)` per defensive cap). **Substrate-honesty design choice (load-bearing)**: the `Side` variant carries BOTH `profile_a_count` AND `profile_b_count` independently — even though `LoftOp::evaluate` enforces equal counts at runtime (rejects `InvalidParameter` if `profile_a.len() != profile_b.len()`), the tag does NOT depend on that validation rule. The constructor handles unequal counts directly, and `for_loft_face_handles_unequal_profile_counts_at_constructor_level` test exercises this directly (`Side { 0, 4, 5 }` produces a finite ID distinct from both `Side { 0, 4, 4 }` and `Side { 0, 5, 5 }`). **A→B ordering is hashed**: swapping `profile_a` and `profile_b` produces different IDs for `Side(i)` (gate test `for_loft_face_distinct_for_swapped_profile_counts`: `Side { 0, 4, 5 }` ≠ `Side { 0, 5, 4 }`). 7-clause stability contract pinned in `LoftFaceTag` docstring: (1) Bottom/Top stable across `length` AND shape-size changes; (2) Bottom/Top categorical (no inner data, matching ExtrudeFaceTag precedent); (3) Side stable across `length` AND coordinate-only profile changes when both counts unchanged; (4) Side breaks across either profile count changing (BOTH counts independently hashed); (5) Side depends on profile-A-count vs profile-B-count ordering; (6) substrate does NOT inspect profile coordinates (rotation / twist / vertex-pairing offset OUT OF SCOPE for v0); (7) no twist-matching implied (future twist param requires new variant or field). 15 lib unit tests added (4 in face_tag.rs: serde round trip, non-exhaustive pattern, distinct edge indices, distinct profile counts; 8 in face_id.rs: deterministic, distinct across tag kinds, distinct across owners, distinct for swapped profile counts, handles unequal counts at constructor level, distinct from extrude/cuboid/revolve under same owner; 3 in loft.rs: brep_provider_returns_n_plus_2_pairs_for_squares, brep_provider_returns_n_plus_2_pairs_for_pentagons, brep_provider_topology_face_ids_are_canonical_emission_order). 4 integration tests added in new `tests/loft_face_identity_smoke.rs`: stable across length changes (3 length values byte-identical 6 face IDs), stable across shape-size changes at same point count (unit square vs 3-unit square IDs match — substrate doesn't inspect coordinates), break when both profile counts change together (square vs pentagon, BOTH profiles change because LoftOp validates equal counts; caps' IDs match per categorical-cap clause but every Side ID is disjoint), distinct across owners. Cross-operator-separator gate tests confirm `b"loft:"` produces disjoint identity spaces from `b"cuboid:"` / `b"extrude:"` / `b"revolve:"` under same owner. Pentagon coordinates used for the integration test: regular pentagon at unit radius `[(1.0, 0.0), (0.309, 0.951), (-0.809, 0.588), (-0.809, -0.588), (0.309, -0.951)]` (5 finite CCW points; passes Polygon2D::new + LoftOp's evaluate-time convexity check). 2026-05-11 06:00:00 - **PHASE 7 D-SWEEP LANDED — 7TH CAD-CORE OPERATOR.** Bounded substrate dispatch mirroring D-Loft / D-Extrude / D-Revolve conventions; no new ADR / no new lint / no new doctrine doc / no new §18 companion. **NEW** `crates/cad-core/src/operators/sweep.rs` (~600L; 21 unit tests + module-doc with full Geometry / Conventions / Restrictions / Capability surface sections): `Polyline3D` open 3D polyline path (private `points: Vec<[f32; 3]>`, public `new(points) -> Result<Self, Polyline3DError>` validating ≥2 points + finite + no coincident adjacent; `points()` / `len()` / `is_empty()` accessors); `Polyline3DError { TooFewPoints, NonFiniteCoordinate, DegenerateSegment }`; `SweepOp { profile: Polygon2D, path: Polyline3D }` arity 0 with `new(profile, path) -> Self` (no length to validate; construction defers to constituent types). **Algorithm**: validate path (≥2 points, finite); validate **monotonic-Z** (`path[k+1].z > path[k].z` strict; principal v0 restriction pinning cap-orientation correctness without path-tangent computation); validate profile (≥3 points, finite, convex via `Polygon2D::convexity`, non-degenerate via `Polygon2D::signed_area`); per-profile winding correction (CCW canonical); generate `n * m` vertices (ring `k` is profile rigidly translated to `path[k]`; profile remains in XY plane at every ring — NOT rotated to follow path tangent); generate index buffer with first cap (-Z normal, fan-triangulated from vertex 0), last cap (+Z normal, fan-triangulated from last-ring offset), and side-wall quads (2 triangles per `(path_segment, profile_edge)` pair). Total: `n*m` vertices / `2*n*(m-1) + 2*(n-2)` triangles. For `m=2` and `+Z`-aligned path the formula collapses to `4n-4` matching ExtrudeOp/LoftOp exactly. **32-byte BLAKE3 structural_hash** over `(b"sweep:" || profile_len_u32 || profile points || path_len_u32 || path points)` — domain separator + interior length-prefix between profile and path so structurally-distinct shapes hash distinct (mirrors LoftOp's profile-A-vs-B separator pattern). **`OpKind::Sweep` + `OperatorNode::Sweep(SweepOp)` variants added**; `as_operator()` match arm extended; `op_kind_non_exhaustive_pattern_match_compiles` extended with `OpKind::Sweep => "sweep"` arm; module-doc anticipated-future-variants set narrows from "Sweep / Fillet" to "Fillet" only. **`crates/cad-core/src/lib.rs`** re-export list extended with `Polyline3D` + `Polyline3DError` + `SweepOp`. **NEW** `crates/cad-core/tests/sweep_smoke.rs` (~50L; 1 integration test): `sweep_square_along_3_point_z_path_through_full_pipeline` chains `CadGraph::begin_operation → graph_mut().add_operator → set_root → commit → graph().evaluate` for unit-square + 3-point z-path 0→1.5→3.0; asserts 12 vertices / 20 triangles / 60 indices / first ring at z=0 / middle ring at z=1.5 / last ring at z=3.0. **21 unit tests in sweep.rs foot**: 4 Polyline3D construction (too-few-points / non-finite / coincident-adjacent / round-trip) + 2 SweepOp construction & arity (new_accepts_valid_inputs / rejects_inputs_for_arity_0) + 3 validation (concave / non-monotonic-Z / zero-z-segment) + 6 geometry (square × 2-point z = 8/12/36 / triangle × 3-point z = 9/14/42 / square × 4-point z = 16/28/84 / xy-drift stair-step still valid 12/20 / cw-profile auto-flipped / top_ring_z_equals_last_path_z) + 4 structural_hash (deterministic / changes-with-path / changes-with-profile / changes-with-path-segment-count) + 2 trait-coverage (op_kind_is_sweep / output_is_labeled_returns_false). The operator-kind tag is a literal byte-string `b"cuboid:"` NOT `OpKind`'s numeric discriminant, so future variant reordering on `OpKind` cannot break stability for callers who already serialized old `BRepFaceId`s. Unit tests cover: owner-id round-trip, owner-id serde via ron round-trip (cad-core uses ron not serde_json), for_cuboid_face determinism, all-six-tag distinctness, owner-change distinctness, domain-separator-makes-id-distinct-from-undecorated-blake3 (proves the domain separator does its job by computing the bare-payload hash without the prefix and asserting inequality), truncation-rule pin (cross-checks the implementation truncates the FIRST 16 bytes via re-computing the full BLAKE3 in the test), face-id serde round-trip, owner zero-vs-max distinctness. **NEW** `crates/cad-core/src/topology/face_tag.rs` (~125L incl. 3 unit tests): `CuboidFaceTag` 6-variant `#[non_exhaustive]` enum in canonical face-emission order **`NegZ, PosZ, NegY, PosY, NegX, PosX`** matching `CuboidOp::evaluate` (verified by reading `crates/cad-core/src/operators/cuboid.rs` lines 114-128 — the `indices` array emits triangles in that exact order; the spec listed `NegX, PosX, NegY, PosY, NegZ, PosZ` alphabetic but the spec ALSO directed "the tag enum's variant order MUST follow the implementation, not the alphabetic hunch" so the implementation order was followed). `discriminant()` const fn returns frozen `u8` 0..5 pinning the BLAKE3 derivation's tag byte. Tests: discriminant-matches-canonical-emission-order pinning the contract; serde round-trip via ron preserves variant; non-exhaustive-pattern-match compiles with wildcard arm. **NEW** `crates/cad-core/src/topology/provider.rs` (~55L; trait-only no tests): `BRepProvider` sibling trait to `Operator` exposing `fn brep_face_ids(&self, owner: BRepOwnerId) -> Vec<(TopologyFaceId, BRepFaceId)>`. Pairs the existing per-tessellation sequential `TopologyFaceId` with the new rebuild-stable `BRepFaceId`. Returned pairs are in canonical face-emission order. Module-doc pins the design choice: this is a **sibling trait** NOT a default-method extension on `Operator` NOT an `Operator: BRepProvider` supertrait bound — preserving (1) v0 implements only for `CuboidOp`, no cascade requirement on other operators; (2) opt-in zero-overhead substrate; (3) future per-operator impls are pure additions. **MODIFIED** `crates/cad-core/src/operators/cuboid.rs`: imports for `topology::{BRepFaceId, BRepOwnerId, BRepProvider, CuboidFaceTag}` + `tessellation::TopologyFaceId`; new `impl BRepProvider for CuboidOp` block (~30L) iterating the canonical-order `[CuboidFaceTag; 6]` constant-array `[NegZ, PosZ, NegY, PosY, NegX, PosX]` and pairing `TopologyFaceId(idx as u64)` with `BRepFaceId::for_cuboid_face(owner, *tag)` via `enumerate().map(...)`. Two new unit tests inside the existing `tests` module: `brep_face_ids_returns_six_pairs_in_canonical_order` (verifies `pairs.len() == 6` + each `face_id.0 == idx as u64` + each `brep_id == BRepFaceId::for_cuboid_face(owner, expected_tags[idx])`) and `brep_face_ids_are_pairwise_distinct` (no two of the 6 BRepFaceIds collide under the same owner). 2026-05-09 16:30:00 - **D-7.2-BETA EXTRUDE B-REP FACE-IDENTITY (VARIABLE TOPOLOGY) EXIT GREEN — SECOND `BRepProvider` IMPL.** Bounded substrate dispatch extending the sub-7.2-α (Cuboid) substrate to `ExtrudeOp` — the second `BRepProvider` impl in cad-core, this time with **variable topology** (a profile of `N` vertices yields `N + 2` faces in canonical emission order Bottom cap → Top cap → Side(0..N-1)). +14 net workspace tests = 11 lib unit (3 in `crates/cad-core/src/topology/face_tag.rs::tests` for `ExtrudeFaceTag` + 5 in `crates/cad-core/src/topology/face_id.rs::tests` for `for_extrude_face` + 3 in `crates/cad-core/src/operators/extrude.rs::tests` for the new `BRepProvider` impl) + 3 integration in NEW `crates/cad-core/tests/extrude_face_identity_smoke.rs`. No new ADR / no new lint / no new doctrine doc / no new sec 18 companion / no `Operator` trait modification / no `Tessellation` / `OperatorNode` / `OperatorGraph` / `Polygon2D` modification / no `CuboidOp` modification (sub-7.2-α impl byte-identical) / no `provider.rs` modification (trait already correct from sub-7.2-α) / no `cad-projection` / `gfx` / kernel integration / no Cargo.toml modification / no D-Fillet prep. **NEW** `crates/cad-core/src/topology/face_tag.rs` extension: `ExtrudeFaceTag` 3-variant `#[non_exhaustive]` enum in canonical face-emission order (`Bottom`, `Top`, `Side { edge_index: u32, profile_count: u32 }`); `discriminant()` const fn returns frozen `u8` 0..2 (Bottom=0, Top=1, Side=2); inner data of `Side` (`edge_index`, `profile_count`) is BLAKE3-hashed NOT used as the discriminant byte. **Load-bearing design choice (substrate honesty)**: `Side` carries BOTH `edge_index` AND `profile_count` so topology changes (square N=4 → pentagon N=5) break face identity by construction — the BLAKE3 input bytes differ. **Stability contract pinned in 4-clause ExtrudeFaceTag docstring**: (1) `Bottom` and `Top` IDs are stable across `length` parameter changes; (2) `Side { edge_index, profile_count }` IDs are stable when both `edge_index` and `profile_count` are unchanged (changing only `length` does not invalidate any side); (3) profile-count changes break `Side` IDs by construction (topology changes are NOT silently preserved); (4) **profile-vertex-order rotation at the same count preserves `Side` IDs** — substrate does NOT inspect profile coordinates; profile rotated `[A,B,C,D]` → `[B,C,D,A]` produces same `Side(0)` ID; this is an explicit limit of the v0 substrate, coordinate-aware identity / rotation detection is OUT OF SCOPE for sub-7.2-β. Unit tests: `extrude_face_tag_serde_round_trip` (Bottom + Top + 3 Side variants via ron); `extrude_face_tag_non_exhaustive_pattern_compiles` (mirrors CuboidFaceTag precedent with `Side { .. }` arm + wildcard); `extrude_side_distinct_for_distinct_edge_indices` (constructor-level — `Side {0, 4}` vs `Side {1, 4}` distinct via PartialEq; same-key equal via PartialEq; `Side {0, 4}` vs `Side {0, 5}` distinct; Bottom/Top/Side all pairwise distinct). **NEW** `crates/cad-core/src/topology/face_id.rs` extension: imports widened to `super::face_tag::{CuboidFaceTag, ExtrudeFaceTag}`; new const `KIND_EXTRUDE: &'static [u8] = b"extrude:"` alongside existing `KIND_CUBOID`; new constructor `BRepFaceId::for_extrude_face(owner, tag) -> Self` with BLAKE3 input layout `DOMAIN || owner.as_bytes() || b"extrude:" || tag.discriminant() || (Side ONLY: edge_index.to_le_bytes() (4 bytes) || profile_count.to_le_bytes() (4 bytes))` truncated to first 16 bytes; for `Bottom` and `Top` the BLAKE3 input ends after the discriminant byte (no inner data) — caps' identity is stable across both `length` AND `profile_count` changes. Unit tests: `for_extrude_face_deterministic` (4 tags including Side {0,4} and Side {7,12} repeated calls return byte-identical bytes); `for_extrude_face_distinct_across_tags` (Bottom + Top + Side {0,4} all distinct under same owner); `for_extrude_face_distinct_across_owners` (4 tags × 2 owners — owner-disambiguation property holds for ExtrudeFaceTag like for CuboidFaceTag); `for_extrude_face_count_change_breaks_side_id` (THE substrate-honesty test: `Side {0, 4}` vs `Side {0, 5}` produce DIFFERENT BRepFaceIds — assert_ne! with explicit failure message "side IDs must NOT be preserved across profile-count changes"); `for_extrude_face_distinct_from_for_cuboid_face_with_same_owner` (cross-operator separator check — `Bottom` (discriminant 0) vs `NegZ` (discriminant 0) under same owner produce different IDs purely because of `b"cuboid:"` vs `b"extrude:"` operator-kind separator, pinning the substrate's load-bearing role for the operator-kind separator). **MODIFIED** `crates/cad-core/src/topology/mod.rs`: module-doc updated from "(sub-7.2-α)" to "(sub-7.2-α + sub-7.2-β)" enumerating both face-tag enums + clarifying v0 scope NON-GOALS now exclude RevolveOp/BooleanOp/LoftOp/SweepOp/TransformOp specifically (Cuboid + Extrude are in scope). Three new unit tests inside the existing `mod tests` block: `brep_provider_returns_n_plus_2_pairs_for_square` (asserts square N=4 yields 6 pairs); `brep_provider_returns_n_plus_2_pairs_for_pentagon` (asserts pentagon N=5 yields 7 pairs); `brep_provider_topology_face_ids_are_canonical_emission_order` (verifies `TopologyFaceId(0)` corresponds to Bottom, `TopologyFaceId(1)` to Top, `TopologyFaceId(2 + i)` to Side(i, 4) for i in 0..4 byte-identically). **NEW** `crates/cad-core/tests/extrude_face_identity_smoke.rs` (~155L; asserts Bottom (index 0) and Top (index 1) IDs MATCH between the two — caps' BLAKE3 input does NOT hash profile_count in, so `ids_sq[0] == ids_pen[0]` and `ids_sq[1] == ids_pen[1]` are CORRECT and EXPECTED per the v0 contract; then nested-loop asserts every Side ID across the two is disjoint via `for sq_side in &ids_sq[2..] { for pen_side in &ids_pen[2..] { assert_ne!(sq_side, pen_side, "side IDs must not collide across topology change"); } }`); `extrude_face_ids_distinct_across_owners` (owners `[0x11; 16]` and `[0x22; 16]` produce disjoint identity spaces, mirrors cuboid_face_ids_distinct_across_owners precedent). **HARD NON-GOALS observed during shaping** (substrate IS the resistance — the spec discipline holds across all expansion-pressure points): no edges / vertices / `BRepEdgeId` / `EdgeTag` enums (sub-7.2-γ); 2026-05-09 17:30:00 - **D-7.2-GAMMA REVOLVE B-REP FACE-IDENTITY (FULL/PARTIAL MODE + SEGMENT-DRIVEN TOPOLOGY) EXIT GREEN — THIRD BRepProvider IMPL.** Bounded substrate dispatch extending the sub-7.2-α (Cuboid) + sub-7.2-β (Extrude) substrate to RevolveOp — the third BRepProvider impl in cad-core, this time exercising a topology axis no prior dispatch has touched: **categorical mode change** (Full vs Partial revolution alters the *face set itself*, not just the face count) plus **segment-driven topology** (segment count change breaks Side IDs by construction). +20 net workspace tests = 15 lib unit + 5 integration; no new ADR / no new lint / no new doctrine / no new §18 companion / no Operator trait modification / no Tessellation / OperatorNode / OperatorGraph / Polygon2D modification / no CuboidOp / ExtrudeOp modification (prior BRepProvider impls byte-identical) / no provider.rs modification (trait already correct from sub-7.2-α) / no cad-projection / gfx / kernel integration / no Cargo.toml modification / no D-Fillet prep / no fourth operator. **crates/cad-core/src/topology/face_tag.rs**: extended with two new public types — RevolveMode 2-variant #[non_exhaustive] enum (Full = 0, Partial = 1) derived from RevolveOp::is_full_revolution() at the BRepProvider impl site (NOT a free parameter), and RevolveFaceTag 3-variant #[non_exhaustive] enum in canonical face-emission order matching partial_path::evaluate_partial (Side walls first, then start-cap fan, then end-cap fan): Side { side_index: u32, profile_count: u32, segment_count: u32, mode: RevolveMode } = 0 (always present in both modes; one per profile edge), StartCap { profile_count: u32 } = 1 (Partial mode ONLY — caps are fan-triangulations of the profile polygon), EndCap { profile_count: u32 } = 2 (Partial mode ONLY). The Side variant carries ALL FOUR fields — this is the load-bearing design choice that ensures three independent topology axes break face identity by construction: (1) mode flips (Full ↔ Partial) at the 359°→360° boundary, (2) segment-count changes (8 → 16 segments) per the substrate's Break IDs across segment-count changes directive — segment count is treated as topology in this identity model, mirroring ExtrudeFaceTag::Side's profile_count, and (3) profile-count changes (square → pentagon). Cap variants carry profile_count ONLY — segment_count and angle do not affect cap geometry (caps are fan-triangulations of the profile polygon), so they are deliberately NOT hashed in (substrate honesty: caps don't over-encode). 6-clause stability contract pinned in the RevolveFaceTag docstring: (1) Side IDs stable across ngle numeric changes within the same mode — within Partial mode, three different angles (45° → 90° → 135°) preserve all face IDs; (2) Side IDs break across mode changes by construction — the mode byte is hashed into the BLAKE3 input; crossing the Full/Partial boundary at 359° → 360° produces disjoint Side IDs; (3) Side IDs break across segment_count changes by construction — same rationale as ExtrudeFaceTag::Side's profile_count; (4) Cap IDs (StartCap, EndCap) are stable across ngle and segment_count changes within Partial mode — caps depend on profile_count only; (5) Cap IDs do not exist in Full mode — BRepProvider::brep_face_ids returns 
 pairs for Full and 
 + 2 pairs for Partial; (6) The substrate does NOT inspect profile coordinates — profile-vertex-order rotation at the same profile_count preserves Side IDs (same v0 limit as ExtrudeFaceTag — coordinate-aware identity is OUT OF SCOPE for v0). Mode is driven by the same `is_full_revolution()` discriminator the BRepProvider impl uses (1e-6 epsilon vs 2pi); the BRep substrate does not recompute the boundary epsilon locally. **LoftOp** (~55L additive impl): `3 * N` edges, same shape as Extrude (Loft is structurally Extrude with a distinct top ring); defensive `n_a.min(n_b)` cap mirrors the BRepProvider impl above (LoftOp::evaluate enforces equal counts at runtime, but profile_a/profile_b are publicly assignable, so taking the minimum removes a panic surface). **Compositional-honesty check load-bearing**: `revolve_full_and_partial_edge_ids_are_disjoint` in revolve_edge_identity_smoke.rs is the gate that proves sub-7.2-gamma`s mode break propagates to edges by construction — Full mode with 8 segments produces 4 edges; Partial mode with 8 segments at angle pi*1.99 produces 12 edges; nested-loop `assert!(!partial_edges.contains(full_edge), "full-mode edge ID leaked into partial-mode set; mode break must propagate to edges")` proves the two sets are disjoint. 2026-05-09 (D-7.2-zeta.zeta Phase 7.2 IMPLEMENTATION.md gate-closure stress test — 100 chains x 10 random rebuilds, deterministic seeded; Phase 7.2 IMPLEMENTATION.md exit criterion CLOSED) - bounded single-agent test-only dispatch in A:\RCAD\RGE\. +7 net workspace tests = 1 main gate test + 6 sanity tests in NEW `crates/cad-core/tests/phase_7_2_gate_closure.rs` (~720L). Main gate test `phase_7_2_gate_closure_100_chains_10_rebuilds_seed_0x7e5a_dead_beef_c0de` runs 100 deterministic-seeded random operator chains x 10 random parameter rebuilds per chain (1000 mutations total) over the full Cuboid + Extrude + Revolve + Loft + Transform substrate. Build path: `generate_random_chain` selects RootKind in {Cuboid, Extrude, Revolve, Loft} via `rng.next_range_u32(4)`, parameterizes the root (Cuboid: width/height/depth in [0.5, 5.0]; Extrude: profile_n in {3..=6} as a regular polygon, profile_radius in [0.5, 3.0], length in [0.5, 5.0]; Revolve: profile_n in {3..=6}, segments in {3..=16}, mode coin-flipped Full or Partial, angle in (0, 2pi] — Full = exactly 2pi, Partial in [0.1, pi*1.9]; Loft: profile_n in {3..=6}, profile_radius in [0.5, 3.0] for profile_a + 1.5x radius for profile_b, length in [0.5, 5.0]), then wraps in 0..=2 Transform layers each with translation in [-5, 5]^3 and scale in [0.5, 3]^3 (identity rotation for simplicity). Build-and-resolve uses `CadGraph::new() / begin_operation / graph_mut().add_operator(OperatorNode::X(op)) / connect / set_root / commit("phase-7-2-gate-closure")` then `brep_face_ids_for_node` + `brep_edge_ids_for_node` against the topmost operator. `generate_random_mutation` decides per-rebuild whether to apply a topology-preserving mutation (numeric-only changes that don't affect the face-tag enum's BLAKE3 input) or a topology-changing mutation (changes that DO break face IDs by construction, propagating to edges). Cuboid roots only ever receive preserving mutations (Cuboid is fixed-topology); Extrude/Revolve/Loft roots get a 50/50 coin-flip between preserving and changing. Preserving mutations: Cuboid width/height/depth resampled; Extrude length OR profile_radius resampled (NOT profile_n); Revolve angle (within current mode) OR profile_radius resampled (NOT profile_n, NOT segments, NOT mode); Loft length OR profile_radius resampled (NOT profile_n). Changing mutations: Extrude/Loft pick a different profile_n in {3..=6}; Revolve picks a different profile_n OR a different segments in {3..=16} OR flips mode (Full<->Partial). Mutations always target the root direct-provider's parameters — Transform-parameter mutations are always topology-preserving and would not exercise the topology-changing branch (sub-7.2-epsilon's smokes already cover those). Boolean / Sweep are NOT in the chain generator (resolver returns `TopologyChangingOperator` for those — sub-7.2-epsilon's smokes cover those error paths). For each rebuilt chain, the test asserts `assert_eq!(rebuilt_faces, initial_faces)` AND `assert_eq!(rebuilt_edges, initial_edges)` for preserving mutations, and `assert_ne!(rebuilt_faces, initial_faces)` AND `assert_ne!(rebuilt_edges, initial_edges)` for changing mutations. Vector-level inequality is the substrate's guarantee — Side faces / all edges ARE disjoint when topology changes; categorical caps (Bottom/Top in ExtrudeFaceTag/LoftFaceTag) intentionally preserve identity per the contract from sub-7.2-beta/delta, so full disjointness cannot be asserted. Coverage gate `assert!(topology_preserving_count >= 100)` AND `assert!(topology_changing_count >= 50)` ensures both branches exercised; recorded counts on fixed seed `0x7E5A_DEAD_BEEF_C0DE`: **623 preserving + 377 changing = 1000 mutations**. Hand-rolled `TinyRng` (xorshift64) with primitives `next_u64` / `next_range_u32` / `next_f32_in_range` / `next_bool` is the entire random infrastructure — no Cargo.toml change permitted; xorshift64 cannot accept seed=0 so the constructor `assert_ne!(seed, 0)` defends against future maintainers changing the constant. The 6 sanity tests on the harness machinery (caught no bugs but exercise the harness on small fixed inputs to catch bugs before the full 1000-mutation gate): `tiny_rng_deterministic_for_fixed_seed` (same seed produces same first 10 outputs); `tiny_rng_rejects_zero_seed` (`#[should_panic(expected = "xorshift64 cannot accept seed=0")]`); `chain_generator_visits_all_root_kinds` (300 trials cover all 4 RootKinds); `apply_preserving_mutation_keeps_topology_counts` (50 preserving mutations on a fixed Extrude N=4 chain — face count stays 6, edge count stays 12, IDs byte-identical); `apply_changing_mutation_alters_topology_counts_or_breaks_ids` (50 changing mutations on the same fixed chain — count differs OR IDs differ); `cuboid_chain_only_uses_preserving_mutations` (50 Cuboid chains x 5 mutations each — all asserted `MutationCategory::TopologyPreserving`). **Honest framing — TopologyEvolution interpretation**: The IMPLEMENTATION.md spec text (line 505) reads "100 operator chains x 10 random parameter rebuilds with face/edge IDs preserved per `TopologyEvolution` enum". `TopologyEvolution` lives in `crate::topo_lineage::types` (D-7.4 prototype substrate from 2026-05-07; `pub enum TopologyEvolution { Preserved, Split, Merged, Deleted, Reinterpreted }` capturing operator-internal face evolution like Boolean clip output). It is orthogonal to D-7.2's identity-stability-across-parameter-rebuilds substrate. This dispatch closes the **rebuild-stability spirit** of the gate; `TopologyEvolution` remains the operator-internal lineage substrate (a separate concern, preserved for future work). The honest framing note appears verbatim in the test file's module-doc, the commit message, and HANDOFF.md's new "What just shipped" entry — future readers should not have to wonder why a D-7.4 enum appears in a D-7.2 gate. **HARD NON-GOALS observed during shaping**: no new substrate (no new IDs, no new resolver functions, no operator changes, no `BRepProvider` / `BRepEdgeProvider` modifications, no enum extensions, no new traits — substrate from sub-7.2-alpha through zeta.epsilon is complete and this dispatch consumes it byte-identically); no `Cargo.toml` modification (no rand / proptest / quickcheck / arbitrary dep — hand-rolled xorshift64 `TinyRng` is the entire random infrastructure); no `OperatorGraph` / `Operator` / `OperatorNode` modification; no `Tessellation` / `topo_lineage` / `cad-projection` / `gfx` / kernel/* modification; no new ADR / lint / doctrine doc / sec 18 companion; no PLAN, IMPLEMENTATION, fileandfolderstructure, versions edits; no prior test files modified (all 9 prior B-Rep integration tests + 4 prior face-identity smokes + face_id directory + face_tag.rs + provider.rs + resolve.rs + edge_id.rs + edge_resolve.rs byte-identical); no `tools/architecture-lints/exemptions.toml` modification; no criterion bench / `#[ignore]` opt-in (regular `#[test]` runs in default cargo test; expected runtime well under 30s on commodity hardware — actual: ~0.4s end-to-end); no mutation of Transform parameters as a topology-preserving test path (sub-7.2-epsilon already covers Transform-parameter-change preservation; mutations always target the root direct-provider's parameters); `Status.md` + `change.md` + `HANDOFF.md` (this entry + sibling status updates). **Verification gates ALL GREEN**: cargo build --workspace -j 2 0 errors / 0 new warnings; cargo test -p rge-cad-core --test phase_7_2_gate_closure --no-fail-fast PASS (7 / 7 tests in ~0.04s — single-binary timing); cargo test -p rge-cad-core --all-targets --no-fail-fast PASS (379 / 379 tests; was 372; +7 net); cargo test --workspace --all-targets --no-fail-fast -j 2 = **2080 / 2080 pass** across 235 binaries (was 2073 / 234 binaries; 2026-05-09 (D-Fillet sub-beta - Add Extrude support to FilletOp - variable-topology consumer of BRepEdgeId) - bounded single-agent substrate-validation dispatch in A:\RCAD\RGE\. +18 net workspace tests = 10 unit tests appended in fillet/extrude.rs::tests + 8 integration tests in NEW crates/cad-core/tests/extrude_fillet_smoke.rs. Sub-beta generalizes the FilletOp consumer pattern from fixed Cuboid topology (sub-alpha) to variable Extrude topology (3*N edges for N-vertex profile). **Internal refactor (Phase 1, behavior-preserving)**: replaces sub-alpha's `edge_tags: Vec<(CuboidFaceTag, CuboidFaceTag)>` field with a unified `chamfer_specs: Vec<ChamferSpec>` carrier where `ChamferSpec { vertex_a: u32, vertex_b: u32, inward_direction: [f32; 3] }` is computed at construction time. The Cuboid constructor `FilletOp::new` now resolves edges to ChamferSpecs via lookup against CUBOID_EDGE_TAG_PAIRS + cuboid_edge_corner_indices + cuboid_face_normal — the chamfer-offset bisector that previously computed at evaluation time now precomputes at construction. **Behavior preservation invariant verified**: all 7 sub-alpha integration tests in fillet_smoke.rs pass byte-identically; all 11 sub-alpha unit tests pass byte-identically. **Phase 2 (additive Extrude constructor)**: NEW `FilletOp::new_for_extrude(upstream: &ExtrudeOp, owner: BRepOwnerId, edges: Vec<BRepEdgeId>, radius: f32) -> Result<Self, FilletError>` mirrors `FilletOp::new` for Extrude upstream. Validates radius/empty-list/edge-presence (same FilletError variants — InvalidRadius, EmptyEdgeSelection, EdgeNotInUpstream); resolves each BRepEdgeId via `upstream.brep_edge_ids(owner)` (the BRepEdgeProvider impl on ExtrudeOp emits 3*N edges in canonical [Bottom-perimeter | Top-perimeter | Vertical-seams] order); maps the canonical edge index back to a `(vertex_a, vertex_b)` pair in the upstream's 2N-vertex layout via `extrude_edge_vertex_pair`; computes the inward chamfer-offset direction from profile-edge geometry via `extrude_chamfer_inward_direction` (which uses `extrude_side_outward_normal` rotating profile-edge vector by -90° for CCW-wound profile). For 4-vertex profile (N=4): canonical_index 0 → (0, 1) bottom-perimeter, 4 → (4, 5) top-perimeter, 8 → (1, 5) vertical-seam — verified concretely in `extrude_edge_vertex_pair_table_correctness`. **Phase 3 (file split)**: fillet.rs grew to 1042L after the additive Extrude constructor + tests, exceeding the 1000L split threshold; split into a `fillet/` directory following the `topology/face_id/` precedent. fillet/mod.rs (409L) holds shared types (FilletError, ChamferSpec, FilletOp struct, accessors, Operator impl with the upstream-agnostic evaluate logic) + 9 cross-cutting unit tests (Operator trait + structural-hash + arity rejection + label-stripping). fillet/cuboid.rs (333L) holds `impl FilletOp { pub fn new ... }` + CUBOID_EDGE_TAG_PAIRS + cuboid_edge_corner_indices + cuboid_face_normal + 11 sub-alpha unit tests (validation, accept-all-12, evaluate, helper-table correctness). fillet/extrude.rs (364L) holds `impl FilletOp { pub fn new_for_extrude ... }` + extrude_edge_vertex_pair + extrude_side_outward_normal + extrude_chamfer_inward_direction + extrude_chamfer_spec + 10 sub-beta unit tests (validation, accept-all-3N, helper-table correctness, evaluate). All three files under 1000L. **Load-bearing tests** in NEW `crates/cad-core/tests/extrude_fillet_smoke.rs` (8 integration tests): (1) `fillet_extrude_edge_ids_remain_valid_across_length_changes` — proves rebuild-stability across topology-preserving length changes; an edge ID captured at length=1 is valid for FilletOp::new_for_extrude against rebuilds at length=2 AND length=0.5; FilletOp structural hashes byte-identical (Fillet's structural hash captures only operator-own parameters, not upstream Extrude length); (2) `fillet_extrude_edge_ids_invalidated_by_profile_count_change` — proves topology-change rejection across profile-count changes; the square's edge[0] BRepEdgeId is NOT in the pentagon's 15-edge set (BRepEdgeId derivation hashes the Side face's profile_count which is 4 vs 5), and FilletOp::new_for_extrude rejects with EdgeNotInUpstream. The two load-bearing tests are the substrate-validation core — they prove the consumer pattern generalizes to variable-topology input. Sub-gamma generalizes the FilletOp consumer pattern to mode-driven topology (Revolve Full vs Partial). **Internal architectural consolidation, FilletUpstream trait extraction**: extracts a `pub(crate) trait FilletUpstream: BRepEdgeProvider` with one method `resolve_chamfer_spec(&self, canonical_index: usize) -> Result<ChamferSpec, &'static str>`. Cuboid + Extrude + Revolve impls live in their respective fillet/{cuboid,extrude,revolve}.rs files; each public constructor (FilletOp::new, FilletOp::new_for_extrude, FilletOp::new_for_revolve) delegates to a shared `FilletOp::from_upstream<U: FilletUpstream>` helper that performs the shared validation (radius / empty-edge-list / per-edge upstream lookup) and per-upstream chamfer-spec resolution. Substrate-doctrine validation: 3-implementation rule earned the abstraction (Cuboid + Extrude + Revolve); the trait is internal architectural consolidation, not a public extension point. **Sub-alpha + sub-beta behavior preservation**: refactor is purely internal restructuring; all 7 sub-alpha fillet_smoke.rs integration tests + all 8 sub-beta extrude_fillet_smoke.rs integration tests + all sub-alpha/beta unit tests pass byte-identically (no test modified, no count change, no behavior change). **Geometry support matrix (v0)**: Cuboid all 12 edges supported (sub-alpha). Extrude all 3N edges supported (sub-beta). Revolve Full: 0 edges supported - all side-side adjacencies are circular paths through `segments` vertices in the tessellation. Revolve Partial: 2N of 3N supported - cap-side adjacencies (canonical n..3n) are clean 2-endpoint edges; side-side adjacencies (canonical 0..n) are circular paths and reject. **Adds FilletError::UnsupportedEdgeGeometry { edge: BRepEdgeId, reason: &'static str } variant + #[non_exhaustive] on the enum**. Construction-time rejection - a constructed FilletOp can never be in a state where evaluation fails on unsupported geometry. Substrate honesty: validation works for ALL valid Revolve edges (BRepEdgeProvider lookup is upstream-agnostic), but only cap-side edges in Partial mode produce chamfer geometry in v0. **Cap-side vertex layout**: at ring 0 (start cap, theta=0) or ring `segments` (end cap, theta=angle), partial-mode tessellation has positions[ring*N + cap_local] / positions[ring*N + (cap_local+1)%N]. **Inward direction algorithm for Revolve cap-side**: centroid-based - compute edge midpoint at ring 0/segments, target the Y-axis at the midpoint's Y-coordinate (RevolveOp is rotationally symmetric around Y), normalize raw direction to magnitude ~0.707 (sub-alpha convention) so structural delta is consistent. **NEW crates/cad-core/src/operators/fillet/revolve.rs** (~349L incl. 11 unit tests). **NEW crates/cad-core/tests/revolve_fillet_smoke.rs** (~221L; 9 integration tests). NEW crates/cad-core/src/operators/fillet.rs (482 lines) introduces FilletOp { edges: Vec<BRepEdgeId>, edge_tags: Vec<(CuboidFaceTag, CuboidFaceTag)>, radius: f32, owner: BRepOwnerId } arity 1 + FilletError { InvalidRadius { radius }, EmptyEdgeSelection, EdgeNotInUpstream { edge } } enum. 2026-05-09 (D-Fillet sub-delta - Add Loft support to FilletOp - input-side consumer contract closed) - bounded single-agent substrate-validation dispatch in A:\RCAD\RGE\. +19 net workspace tests = 10 unit tests in NEW crates/cad-core/src/operators/fillet/loft.rs::tests + 9 integration tests in NEW crates/cad-core/tests/loft_fillet_smoke.rs. Sub-delta closes the input-side consumer contract by adding the fourth direct-provider variant: `impl FilletUpstream for LoftOp` + `FilletOp::new_for_loft`. Loft has the same Bottom + Top + N Sides face structure and 3N clean 2-endpoint edges as Extrude (sub-beta); the chamfer geometry adapts Extrude's face-normal-bisector approach to Loft's two-profile vertex layout (profile_a at bottom ring positions[0..N], profile_b at top ring positions[N..2N]). **Profile pairing convention (load-bearing)**: v0 inherits LoftOp's `profile_a[i]` <-> `profile_b[i]` pairing exactly. **No twist matching, no rotation alignment, no coordinate-aware vertex correspondence is introduced by this dispatch**. If LoftOp ever extends to support twist or vertex correspondence, the chamfer geometry will need to be revisited; until then, the i-to-i convention is the substrate's contract. **Consumer matrix closure** (after sub-delta lands, FilletOp consumes BRepEdgeId from all four direct providers): Cuboid (sub-alpha, 12 of 12 edges chamferable; fixed topology); Extrude (sub-beta, 3N of 3N edges chamferable; variable profile count); Revolve (sub-gamma, 2N of 3N edges in Partial mode; 0 in Full mode; circular paths reject); Loft (sub-delta, 3N of 3N edges chamferable; two-profile, i-to-i pairing). The input-side consumer contract is now proven across the provider set. The next architectural conversation - output-side identity for FilletOp (impl BRepProvider / BRepEdgeProvider) - begins after this lands; it is NOT the next dispatch. **NEW crates/cad-core/src/operators/fillet/loft.rs** (~402L incl. 10 unit tests; sole modification to fillet/mod.rs is the single-line `mod loft;` declaration alongside existing mod cuboid;/extrude;/revolve;). All 3N Loft edges are chamferable in v0; no UnsupportedEdgeGeometry variant is ever returned for Loft inputs (mirrors Extrude). **Bottom-perimeter edge i**: bottom face normal (0, 0, -1) + profile_a's side normal at edge i; inward bisector = -(bottom + side)/2. **Top-perimeter edge i**: top face normal (0, 0, 1) + profile_b's side normal at edge i; inward bisector = -(top + side)/2. **Vertical seam (Side(i) cap Side((i+1) mod N))**: average of four side-normal contributions across both profiles' adjacent edges (profile_a's edge i + profile_a's edge (i+1) mod N + profile_b's edge i + profile_b's edge (i+1) mod N); inward bisector = -(sum_of_four_normals)/4. Magnitude convention: half-bisector (~0.707) matching sub-alpha/beta. Defensive `n_a.min(n_b)` pattern mirrors sub-7.2-zeta.delta's BRepEdgeProvider impl on LoftOp (LoftOp::evaluate enforces equal counts but profile_a/profile_b are pub fields; min cap removes a panic surface for mid-mutation through the pub fields). **NEW crates/cad-core/tests/loft_fillet_smoke.rs** (9 integration tests). Four load-bearing sub-delta tests: (1) `fillet_loft_edge_ids_remain_valid_across_length_changes` - proves rebuild-stability across topology-preserving length changes; an edge ID captured at length=1 is valid for FilletOp::new_for_loft against rebuilds at length=2 AND length=0.5; FilletOp structural hashes byte-identical (Fillet's hash captures only owner+edges+radius, not upstream Loft length). (2) `fillet_loft_edge_ids_remain_valid_across_coordinate_changes_with_same_n` - proves coordinate-only changes preserve edge IDs (same profile_count, different XY values; substrate doesn't inspect coordinates per D-7.2-zeta.delta). (3) `fillet_loft_edge_ids_invalidated_by_profile_count_change` - proves topology-change rejection across profile-count changes; the square's edge[2] BRepEdgeId is NOT in the pentagon loft's 15-edge set (LoftOp enforces equal profile counts so changing topology means changing BOTH profiles together: sq×sq -> pen×pen); FilletOp::new_for_loft rejects with EdgeNotInUpstream. (4) `fillet_loft_distinct_owners_produce_disjoint_specs` - mirrors sub-alpha/beta/gamma owner-disjointness pattern (face IDs hash owner bytes into derivation, so distinct owners produce disjoint edge ID sets); FilletOp::new_for_loft rejects an edge captured against owner_x when caller passes owner_y. Other 5 integration tests: `fillet_validates_loft_edge_ids_against_upstream` (all 12 edges of square loft accepted; 3*N=12 for N=4); `fillet_rejects_unknown_loft_edge_id`; `fillet_loft_rebuild_produces_same_structural_delta_across_lengths` (linearity check, +2 verts +6 indices regardless of length); `fillet_loft_through_operator_graph_evaluates_correctly` (end-to-end Loft -> Fillet through CadGraph evaluates to 10 vertices + 14 triangles + 42 indices, structurally identical to the Cuboid -> Fillet result); `fillet_loft_zero_radius_rejected`. The 10 unit tests in fillet/loft.rs::tests cover: validation (new_for_loft_rejects_zero_radius, new_for_loft_rejects_negative_radius, new_for_loft_rejects_non_finite_radius covering NAN+INFINITY, new_for_loft_rejects_empty_edge_list, new_for_loft_rejects_unknown_edge_id); accept paths (new_for_loft_accepts_single_bottom_perimeter_edge, new_for_loft_accepts_all_3n_edges); helper-table sanity (loft_edge_vertex_pair_table_correctness verifies for N=4: canonical_index 0->(0,1), 1->(1,2), 2->(2,3), 3->(3,0) bottom-perimeter; 4->(4,5), 5->(5,6), 6->(6,7), 7->(7,4) top-perimeter; 8->(1,5), 9->(2,6), 10->(3,7), 11->(0,4) vertical-seam); evaluation (evaluate_one_loft_edge_adds_2_vertices_and_2_triangles, evaluate_three_loft_edges_linear_growth). **HARD NON-GOALS observed during shaping** (substrate IS the resistance - central success criterion): no twist matching / rotation alignment / coordinate-aware vertex correspondence (v0 inherits LoftOp's i-to-i profile pairing exactly);
